The treasury of health conteynyng many profitable medycines gathered out of
Hypocrates, Galen and Auycen, by one Petrus Hyspanus and translated into
Englysh by Humfre Lloyd^ who has added thereunto the causes and signs of
every disease, with the Aphorisms of Hypocrates, and Iacobus de Partybus
redacted to a certain order according to the members of man's body, and a
compendiouse tabl^ conteynyng the purginge and confortatyue medycynes, with the
exposicyo^ of certain names and weyghtes in this book contained with an
epistle of Diocles unto king Antigonus.

Ecclesiast.xxxvii. The Lord has created Physycke of the earth, and he that
is wise will not abhor it.

To the Gentil hearted Reader Humfrey Lloyde.
Although diverse learned me^ of no less judgment then practyse, have
berebefore translated and set forth sundry books, containing the most wholesome
and profitable precepts of Physic, wherein they seem to have openid and at
large declared al such things as seemed necessary and expedient to be had and
known in this our vlgare English tongue: yet never thelesse, I calling to
memory the notable s^ntence of Cicero, that every man is not alonly borne for
him self bu^ chifely to profit his native Country then his parents,
afterward his children and friends, seeking a means whereby I might profytte
this my natyue Country, thought it best to translate this little treatise which
was gathered out of the works of the most noble and Ancient phisicions
Hipocrates, Galene, Dioscorides, and Auicen by one Petrus Hispanus which
(although he chanced in a barbarous and rude time) was a man of great
knowledge and long practyse unto which work conteyninge alonly ye simple and
bare practyse, I did add before every chapter as brefely as I could, the
causes and signs of the sicknesses and dyseases, trustyng thereby both to
gratifye and somewhat ease the pains of the reader so that he n^de not ^lles
where to seek the causes and signs of such diseases whose remedies were
contained in this book, and upon that consideration I did also translate and
add herunto the Aphorysmes of Hipocrates redacted unto such an order yt as the
members of man's body be disposed to receive some one disease and some
another, so the Aphorisms, which entreat of eueri disease that may happen to
that membre be gathered together into one chapter beginning at the head and
so in order to the far: and also because men often times desire to know the
names and properties of compounde medicines, I did translate a little book of
such compoundes drawn out of mesue by one Iacobus de partibus, which work
I have redacted to the self same order that the aphorisms be in and
furthermore because I would gratify the reader, and would not he should be
ignorant in the names and weyghtes herin contained. I have hereunto added two
tables, of the which the first does brefly express such symples and
compoundes as do either comfort or purge any disease or hurtful humor
infectynge any member of man's body, and the second expounds certain general
names of medecines and weyghtes commonly mentioned in this book and thereupon
have made an end of this rude and simple work, employng my ^ole labor and
dylygence to set the same furthe as truly and as nigh the authors mind as I
could, not thinking but that there do some faults remain therein both because
the barbarous and arabicke terms which the author does chyefly use, and of the
diverse and sundry opynions of most notable and well learned Phisicions as well in
the names as in ye natures of herbs and simples, and especially that we be
either ignorant or destytute of Englysh names for a great sort of them, yet I
did as nigh as I could follow Dioscorides and in such things as I could not
find in him I did confer Fuchsius, Ruellius and Dorstemius together, and
followed the judgment wherein they did al or the most part of them agree, and in
the Englyshing thereof I and al other which intend any such work are much
beholden to Master Wyllyam Turner, who with no small d^ligence has in both
his herballes most truly and syncerly s^t forth the names and natures of
diverse h^rbes, unto whose judgment and correccio^ and all other learned in the
most necessary science of Physycke, do I submyt this little work and treatise,
desiring them most hartly to take in good worth this my first labor and to
accept my good will, not thynkyng it to be done to hurt any man, knowing what
a perylous thing it is for them that be not learned both in the complectyons of
men, Age, Regions, and time of the year, with the knowledge of the Orygyne and
causes of the diseases, to take upon them the cure of any pacient and that
rather they shall do hurt then good with the sole and only practyse thereof
except they do thereunto add great knowledge and perfyte judgment had with
paynfull study and long practyse, therefore I would that all such rash and
temerariouse persons should perfectly know, that it was never my mind or will
that this work should be set forth to maintain there fylthy lucre and blind
boldness, but ^hefely to be a toke^ and sign of the entye^ de^yre I have to set
forth the thing which should ^e acceptable and pleasant to the Reader, and ^lso
I would that it should be for ye use and pro^yte of such honest persons as will
modest^y and discretelye (either in time of necessyty ^hen no learned Physician
is at hand, or else ^onferryng with some learned man and using (...) council)
mynister the things herin contained and go about the practice thereof, and upon
these most honest and godly co^syderacyo^s, I take upon me this heavy burden
and hard prouynce, therefore I shall most hartly desire the gentle reader to
pardon my audacity and bear with my sclende^ judgment, and not to despise this
simple work because it is not garnished with colors ofrethorik and fine
polyshed terms, but rather to consider that Physike is an art content^ only
to be plainly and distinctlye taught and nothing desirous to be adourned and
decte with eloquence and gay painted sentences, wher^fore I trustyng to the
syncer and indifferent^ judgment of the reader, do entyerly desire him to pray
with me to him that created physick^ of the earth, and commanded that we
should honor the physycion, to preserve this Realm^ of England in most
prosperouse and contynuall health, and to endow the inhabitan^tes thereof, with
perfyte understanding and the most desired knowledge of his holy word. Amen.

Places of scripture which seem to make for the praise of Physyke.
MOses brought forth Israel from the reddesee and they went to the
wilderness of sur, Exodi. 1^.
and they went three days in the wylldernesse and could find no water, and at
the last they came to mara but they could not drink of the waters for ye
byttern^s thereof, and Moses cried unto ye lord and he showed him a tree, and he
cast it into ye waters and they waxed sweet.

Also if you r^de over the.xiii.xiiii,xv, chapters of Leuiticu^ (where the
prestes be taught to dyscerne the Leprosy from all other dyseases) you shall
find many things that make for the praise of Physycke.

H^zekish was sick to the death, and after he had prayed to the lord he sent
Isayahe unto him, Regist. 4. cap. 10.
who put a lump of fygges upon the sore and he recoueryd.

Helyf^us the Prophet healed the naught and bitter waters of Ierycho and the
barennesse of the ground, Reg. 4 chap. 4.^
with castyng salt into the spryng thereof, he healed also Naaman of his
leprosy and the potage that was made of collyqu^ntyda.

The heart is glad of a sweet ointment and savor, Pro. 27. Tobi. 6.
but a stomach that can give good counsel rejoices a man's neighbor.

The angel said unto Tobias, take out the bowels of this fysh and as for the
heart, ye gall and the liver keep them by the for these things ^re necessary for
medecyne.

For the falling of the Hear.
The Causes.
THe falling of the Hear is of two kinds, of the which the one is called
alopecya which is caused thrughe the malignite of vytiouse and noughty Humores
which rote and corrupt the rotes of the Hears whereby they fall away. The
other is called Deflunium capillorum and comes of ye rarytie of the skyne and
lack of the Humore by the which ye hear be come forth and nourished for the
relaxatyon and losnesse of the Skin is the cause why they be not steadfast and
want of their humor does extenuat the same whereby they do fall away.

The Signs.
The signs or tokens be plain enough for in the first, the hear is more
lose in one place then in an other, and in the second they fall in all places
like.

Remedies.
Diosc. Isac.
IF thy hears fall, make lie of ye Ashes of Culuer, dounge and wash thy head,
it is prouyd.

So do walnut leaves beaten with Bears sewet, restore ye hears that be
plucked away.

Seth the leaves of an Oak and the mydle rynd thereof in wa^er and wash thy
head, it is proved.

The ashes of little Frogs burnt Do cure the falling of the hear.

The ashes of Gootes dounge, myngled with oil, Galen,
does engender hear.

The Decoctyone of a Mallowe Rote in water makes the scurffe of the head fall
of, if thy head be washed in that water, it is proved.

The water of the decoction of ye myddle rynde of an elm thy head being often
washed therein, Galen
does the same.

Wormewoode stamped and laid to the temples does quickly remedy the pain in
the head. Macer.


Stamp Parsley with the blood of an Hog, let them sethe in white wine and
afterward let it be streyned through a cloth over cold water, and let the
Fat that flyteth or swimmith above be gath^red together and mengl^d with the
yolke of of a sodden egg and Mastike and Cummin and let the bare place be
anointed there with and there will hear grow quyckely, it has been prouyd.

Annoynte the place with raw Honey and sprynkle it over with the (...) over
with the Ashes of a grene Lacerte burnt, it enge^dreth much hear it is prouyd.

Diosc.
The blood of a Tortois, if ye bare place be anointed there with enge^dreth
much hear and curethe the Leprye.

The same does the Shell of the Snayle being brent.

Gerard.
The Milk of an Ass does make black the hear after a wounderfull manner.

Burn Barley bread with Salt, and mengle it with Bears sewet, and anoint on
what place so ever thou will and the hears will grow there.

The Joyce of Sloes and Ynke the utter rind or shale of a Nutte brayde and
tempered with vinegar so that they be moist, let them be applied for an
ointment and they do make the pacientes hear black.

The Ashes of a Goats clawe, menglid and beaten with Pytche, remedieth the
falling of the hear.

Let thy head be washed with Dogs piss, and thou shall not be bald

Make lie of the ashes of the wod of Iuye, ye rind first pulled of wash an old
ma^s head therwyth and his hears shall be yelow two months space after.

These things following make hear to grow after Auicenius opinion first Oil
wherein a kind of flies called Cantharides be sod and boyld does greatly dry
the fleme and afterward let these be applied which follow. Oil of Eggs,
Auicen.
bears sewet, Ashes of the herb called Condise or Lanary and of the pintle
and spleen of an Ass, the ashes of the ears and bellye of an Hare burnt, ye
ashes of Laudatiu^ or Cist sage of sothernwod, of Teintworte and the ashes of
burned filberts and also of wal^uttes, oil of Radyshe and Bayberys.

A Lacert and horse leches, minglyd together with the Oil called Laudanum and
let the place be anointed therwyth, and for a suerty the hear will grow, it is
prouyd.

Galen.
Burn the head, of a Fox together with the skyne unto ashes, and boil a
Lacert (the head being cut o^) in oil mightilye a hole day, and anoynte and
sprinkle that place with ye ashes where you will have hear grow. The same
thing workithe the ashes of Gotes doung, or of the clawe of a Got.

Burn a quycke Snayle upon a Tile and crushe it to ashes with.. of alume and
as much Mary of a Dear, sethe these in Wine and a anoint the baldnes. The same
thing does the ashes of Bees myxte with oil.

Euphorbiu^ myngled with oil is wonderful good.

To take away Hear.
The Causes.
IT is a comin saying that if the one contrary be known the other is plain
and evident. Auicen.
So like wise he that knows why the hear fallethe or is little in quantytie,
is not ignorant why the Hear is much in quantytye and steadfast, which
comes of the multitude of incorrupt humors and thycknesse of the Skine of the
head with streytnesse of the holes through the which the hear grows.

The Signs.
There is no declaracyon of the tokens necessary if a man do either se or
feel the head.

Remydes.
IF thou will yt the hear should never grow up again, pluck them up by the
rotes, and anoint the place with the blood of a back or with the blood of a
little Frogge, it is proved.

Put also to the place horse leches taken out of the standing water and
dressed with strong Uineger.

The ashes of a Colewortes stalk made in a plaster lets the growing up
of hears, it is prouyd.

The milk of a Bitche if the place be anointed therwt will not suffer ye hear
to grow. Galen.
The same affirmith Galene also, of ye blood of a bitche.

Let the joyce of a Gourde, well and delygently mengled with water be put on
the bare place.

Lapdanu^ the gum of an Iuy tree Emetes Eggs Arsenicke and Uineger bound to
the place whereto ye will apply the^ and there will never hear grow.

Put the ashes of a grene frogge brent in a bathe and all the hears y^ be
washed of ye bathe will fall away it is prouyd.

The Branne of Lupines or penny bean laid on the hearye place, Isac.
will make the hear to fall, and will not suffer other to grow.

The Joyce of Fumitorie myxte with gum of Arabyke and laid on the place the
hears first plucked out by the rotes will not parmytte the hears to grow.
Dioscor.


Been flower laid to the preuye me^bres of a child, will not suffer the hear
to grow.

The things that let the growing up of hear after Auice^ be these opi^m,
Henbane, Auicen.
the roughnes or cot^on yt is found in Fleworte the blood ^f water Frogs, of
a water snaile ^ of a Rere mouse, and the oil of ^he Decoccyon of a little
grene la^ert and the earth called Cymolea

nape of the neck be washed and afterward anointed with the oil of the
Decoction of Rape Uielet or Sowbread for it heals myghtly.

Let the breaking out of the ring worm of the head be washed with strong

Against forgetfulness or drousynes.

The Causes.
THis disease is called in Greek of the effect Lethargus and in latin veternus
and is caused of cold and putrified phlegm which has made cold, and filled
the brain.

The Signs.
The Lythargye comes with great sluggishnes and such desire of sleep as cannot
be eschued, with great oblyuion, and forgetfulness so that they can skant tell what
they have done, nor make answer when they be spoken unto.

Remedies. Capi. iiii.
Against this disease of forgetfulness apply Rewe and red myntes with oil and
very strong Uineger unto thy nosthrilles. Galen. Co^stan.


Burn thine own heat and mingle it with Uineger and a little pytche and apply
it to thy nosethrilles, Constable.
for it wou^derfully stirs and quickneth yt persons diseased with
forgetfulness. The ligthes of an hog laid unto the head being shaven is very
good

The blood of a Tortoys anointed on ye forehed is of much valor

The gal of a Crayne being made warm in a leaden vess^l does thoroughly and
lyghtlye stir up the deseased body if y^ nape of his neck be anointed
therwyth.

Fume made of Roes lether, does myghtyly sterre him up.

Fume of Kyds skins does quicken forgetful persons and those yt be infected
with the falling syknes and weme^ also that have their flowers stopte.

The sent or smell of Dog fennel, takes away sleep.

Grynd Mustard sede with Uineger, and rub it myghtyly on the pla^tes of the
feet, and it does quicken forgetful persons.

Sauery beaten and sodden in Uineger and laid in form of a plaster to the
hinder part of the head does merrily awaken those yt are heavy with sleep.

Nothing does better quicken forgetful persons then the smoke of a man's hear.

A drink made of Anacardiu^ is a peculiare remedy is this desease. Galen,


The smoke of Galbanum or of an h^rtes horn is best of al things

The skin of an Hare burnt and the ashes thereof droncke with calament heal
the lytargie.

For the Frensye.
The Causes.
THe Phrenisye comes of great abundance of blood or choler fyllyng up the
brains or paunicules thereof. Which choler if it be adust engenders a most
peryllouse and peruiciouse phrenesy.

The Signs.
They which have the frenesye be troubled with a contynual fever and madness
with great watchinges and little sleep, and when they wake they roar and cry
and cannot tell what they say or do, and if it come of blood they laughe, of
choler they fight and braule and ska^t be ruled without Cords or Chains.

Remedies. Ca. v.
First let ye matter be put back with the joyce of Playntayne or morel and
Uyneger anointyng the temples therewith, then make a coife or cappe of wax
terebintine and womans milk and put it upon the head, for it will ease the
pains and provoke the pacyent to sleep.

Constable.
Let the fume of the matter be drawn downward with a suppository or clister,
and with moderate rubbyng of the hands and feet, then put a sponge dipped in
the decoction of Henbane or a whelpe or a cock rypt over ye belly upon the
head, or ye lyghtes of a swyne, also bynd the arms and legs of the pacyent,
and let him smell Opium, camphory, Henbane, Basyl, Saffru or wax mingled with
Rose water, afterward anoynte the ears, eyes and nodle with mirth, storax,
Castoreum, or wash, the head, with Henbane or Smalage that have be^ sod in
sweet wine

Make an oyntme^t of Dogfenel detain and oil of Roses, and anoint his head
therwyth and it shall cause him to sleep.

Also take of Opium. ii. of leven.ii. well beatyn with honye and vinegar and
anoynte the Pulses there with.

Make a plaster of Opium, henbane sede, and Sugar, myngled in the joyce of
lettys and lay it to his forehead.

Make a suppositori of Opium and oil of Uyolettes.

White Popie, and Henbane seed distempred with the white of an Egg and laid to
the forhead provoke sleep.

It is very good to let blood of ye vain which is in the myddel of the
forhead.

Take..i. of opium..ii. of black popy and distempre them with populeon and the
milk of a woman that gives suck to a wenche and lay it to the foreheade.

The wax of the pacyentes ear, given him in drink causes him to sleep.

Seth Henbane in sweet wine and wash therewith thy ears temples and nose
thrilles, and it provoke sleep. The hot lights of a goat clapped to the
head takes away the frenesy so does a Spo^ge dipped in warm wine and put to the
left Pappe,

It is very good to anoint ye forhead with oil of Roses, and to put a horsleche
to the forhead.

Constable.
Safron in all meats provoke sleep.

Lay to the pacyents head Saffro^ Mandrage and Opium and he shall sleep.

Galen
If the head be anointed with oil of Roses, Dogfenell, and Castoru^, it swageth
the pains and causes the pacyent to sleep. Galene.

Sprinckle the powder of Mandrage and Arsenike upon a shaven head, and the man
shall sleep.

If the face be washed with hot water of the Decoctyon of Popy ye pacyent

it has been prouyd.

If the Fra^tyke man have is head anointed with Castoreum, without dout he shall

If thou would, cause a man to sleep take Opium, Henbane, Plantayn Popy, and the

another sponge in Uineger and hold it to his nose.

For the head ache.
The Causes.
THis disease called in Greek cephalalgia and in arabike Soda comes somtymes
of great multitude of humors contained, in the head and sometimes of an
outward cause as of heat of the son of cold, of drunkenness, and of a
stripe, which be also diverse and sunday, but because the aucthore is so short
in his remedies (and I entende to write nothing here but that shall be
necessary for the understanding of him) I will pass the^ ou^r at this time.

The Signs.
Great pains in the head.

Remedies. Cap. vi.
THe joyce of ground yuie cast into the nosethrilles purges the head and
takes away the pain.

This does purge the head wonderful well in every kind of head ache. take wax,
Masticke Pellitory, mustard seed, town cresses, Nigella romana, Stauisager,
Cynamon, and of black and white, hellebore, of either.ii. ounces let these be
well pu^ned and put in a bag of lynen clothe, then let ye pacye^t fasting hold
this bage i^ his mouth and chaw it betwixt his teeth, Gerard.
and after wash his mouth with warm wine and Honey.

When al remedies fayl a cantery in the hinder part the head helps

Against the Rewme.
The Causes.
A Great multitude of cold humors in the brain wych fall down to the nose and
throat.

The Signs.
This disease is sone known and especyally in cold weder.

Remedes. Capi. vii.
IF the Rewme come of a could cause lay hot Calame^t or runnynge Time bruysed
to the head.

Diosc.
An emplayster made of Garlike, cloves and leaves stops ye humore causynge
the rewme.

Ysope bruiled in ye embres and so laid to ye head, stops ye Rewme. A
little bag full Darnel salt and anyse laid to the head is very good

does remove from the brain al superfluouse humors.

Against the turn or daselyng^ in the head.
The Causes.
A Gross and thycke humore in ye brain, from the which rise vaporouse

rose water be consumed, then cole it, and with the same blood mengle the
pouders above specified, and they shall be kept in their lively strength. This
has been proved.

The wine of the decoction of rue unto ye third part dropped into ye eyes

Of the pain of the Ears.
The Causes.
Going or riding in cold wynd^s, or bathing in cold wat^r and sum times it
comes of a hot inflammation.

The Signs.
Great pains in the ears either with hete or cold.

Remedies. Capi. xiii.
THe joyce of wild Cucu^mere leaves, Diosc.
takes away ye grefe of the ears.

Take and put the grene wood of an Asshe in the fyere, and save the licour that
comes out at the end of the same and put it into thine ears it causes the
pain of ye ears to cease and amendeth the hearing.

Stamp earth worms, the eggs of Emetes and ye leaves of Rue together and
being sodden in oil strain them and let faull one drop of that oil being
warm into thine ear it restores again the hearing, being ons lost.

Put oil and scalion seed together, and me^gle thereto the joyce of lekes, and
wormewod, and womans milk sees them over the coals and strain it, and put
one drop into thine ear and stop it fast with silk in the morning, after six
hours, take it out, and turn the sore ear downward and wash it gently, it
is a goodly experymente.

Item in a hot cause, lettis made in a plaster is much worth. Hemp tow dipped
in the white of an egg is very good it is proved.

Item worms of the earth sta^pte with Rose water and applied to the ear are
very good also.

Item hot water with woman's milk only, applied for a plaster is of much
efficacy.

Rogerus.
Item if a little stone or a grain or any such like thing faull into a man's

ryndes of nuttes or of the leaves of a peache tree.

Arype aple yt has a good savor is to be applied unto the ear being warm
somewhat opened on the lower part that fasteyneth to the tree and in the
morning you shall find there a worm al to pieces through the savor of the apple.

very much.

ears.

Put the joyce of Sengrene, oil olive, the joyce of a leeke, the milk of of a

nights setting the mouth open, it is said to restore the hearing wounderful
well.

The gall of a Got put into the ear with joyce of a Leeke, takes away the

Gross and slymy blood changed (...) white phlegm, or to melancholye.

The skin to be spotted like (...) a Snake.

For the toth ache.
The Causes.
The ^ynowes being very hot or cold or great quantity of humors, falling from
the head to the gummes.

The Signs.
The pain is known well enough

For bledynge at the nose.

A vain or arteri opened or bro^en within the nose with great abu^^ance of
blod, or to much labouri^g.

The Signs.
To blede at the nose.

Like is said of veruen.

Gross humors flowyng to the synowes.

Remedies. Capi. xvii.
PArali^is is a sickness called the Palsy: wherein either all the body or one
member or many me^bres be mortyfyed and be depryued of feling and moving, it
happenith either of an impostume stopping the rotes of the sinowes, yt they
being deprived of y^ lively spirits which serve for them be come dead, or else
of the Fleumatyke humor gross^ and undigested which stoppith the said places
some time of a stroke or faul, whereby the joints of the back bone ar loused
and the synowes which come from the neck or nape of the head, ar stopped other
while the synowes and the rotes of them hu^te with a bruyse engenders the
palsy, and specially in a old man.

bleder full of the decoction of Camomyll, Honye, and Fenegreke and such lyk^.

sorer attractions because that layeng to of things euaporatynge, wo^keth only
the increase of pain, for all medecynes euaporatynge and draw from the
inward part by subtyllynge the humore and increasyth Rewme by openinge the
ways, use therefore Maturatiues Ingrossatyues, and Diuisiues, as these
followyng, Root of Holyhoke, dry Lyquyrys, rise, the Milk or joyce of Wheat
steyped in water a certain day^s, and Lynesede, Fenigreke, Fleworte, Pease,

warm things I have receuyd this knowledge of a certain man and worthy
credyte, yt this is a most sure remedy and with out danger because it makes
the cause and humor of the pleurify to come forth.

Of the colyke and the pain called yliaca.
The Causes
The Colyeke comes of gross* and slimy humors or of wynd contained in the gut
colone, and yliaca is engendered of raw and corupt meats specially fat, and by
drinking cold drink after great heat.

The Signs
Grypynges and pain in the utter part of the belly with restriction thereof, and
belchynge and lothynge of meat do signifye the Colycke, and yliaca is when the
pains and swellyng is in the small guts with belchynge and murmuring in the
belly.

Remedies. Capi. xxviii.

grefe wo^derfullye.

takes the grefe away incontinent.

mengle with molte^, pitche, and suete meltid, lay it to whote, it is very good.

resoluith wyndines and sl^my humors this have I prouyd.

In Apostem, or gross humors therein contained.

fenell roots, Percely. i. strain these same and use them, and after thou have

Anyse, of Fenell, Gotes dounge, of al like much let the^ be myngled and make a
powder thereof, afterward give a little quantyty of seen, and a garicke, with
Uermilyon it is very good against the stoppyng of ye liver and heals them
that have ye dropsye of a cold cause.

Such alike drink as this does very well op^n the stoppynges in the liver of
a hot cause.

To stop the flours
The Causes
The veins broken or opened, erosyons in the matrix or losinge of a child.

The Signs.
Change of color, swellyng in the feet and lack of appetyte.

Remedies. Capi. xlvii.
IF the Flowers will not cease in there natural time, make a pessarie of goats
dou^ge, and the joyce of shepherds purse or ribwort or Pla^tayne, and put it
into the matrix.

Yarowe stampid with the water of the decoctyon of ypoquistidos, and the
flouers of pomgranate, stops wonderfulli.

Make abath of these herbs Pla^tayne, Shepherds purse, wild Tasill, and the
middel rind of an Oak, and afterward use this pessary. Take the powder of a
hearts horn, Ipoquistidos, Acacia, bole armeniake, new plaster, wax, Talowe
of a Got, and of ye which remaynethe make a plaster to the raynes and share
and it stops Flowers on warrinsise. Likewise make a bathe of the rind of an
Oak, quicken beres or service, and plaster, this is of great efficacy.

As many graynes as a woman does drink of Coryander sede, so many days shall
the Flowers be stoppid.

Apessary or powder of ceruse or white lead minglid with powder of smallage,
does meruelousli stop the Flowers.

The joyce of Lekes stops both the flowers and after burden,

Coral drunk stops the flowers, so does the ashes of brent acornes cast
into the matrix dry and heal al fylthy and nociue hummours.

Acatia made in a pessarye is very good for the same, likewise agreat ventose
laid to the papes and kept a hole hour.

Rybwort drunk or made in a pessary stoppithe al flux of matrix and there is
no medicine comparable unto this.

The sede or rote of water lylly has a peculiar virtue.

The water found in an holowe Oak is g^od with Rain water for the same rso is
water of Pulyol drunk.

A decoctyon of Akorne shales does me^uelously enclose the matrix, and so does
a pessary of morell.

Sanct John's herb drunk, does stop utterly both whyt and Red flux
Cynabarys of some men callid dragons blood has a maruelouse strength to stop
the matrix.

For the mother.
The Causes.
Much a bundance of humors with stopping of the flowers, or the co^tencyon and

The Signs.
Sadness, pal^ color sluggishnesse, weakn^sse in the legs, and in the

crampes in the legg^s.

For the Gout.
The Causes.
Much surfettinge and dronkenesse, to much accompaingin with women, imoderat
excercice, long sta^dynge, and such like,

The Signs.
Great pains and swellinge in the joints chyeflye in spryngtyme and heruest.

sycknes long hanging upon a man before, if it be vsyd.

Be sure of this one thing that in some cause medicines yt are made (except
they be purging, or breking or at the lest except some sufficient euacuacio^
of ye matter go before) do not greatly h^lpe, therefore let the hot humor be
purgyd with an electuary made of the joyce of rosys.

Let those pacientes be well ordered and warely and let the matter be by little,
and little purged, that the nouryshynge virtue be not dystroyd, for in Pills,
many things are received that draw with vyolence, as euphorbium,
harmodactill, Colloquiti^a, Turbith, scamony, which all are as it were poison,
and therefore indiscreetly mynystred causes faintness through the debilitie of
vital sperites, in that nature cannot with stand the mattre, and such things
are never mynystred except they have stand setteled a good while after
commixtion, and full ordrynge, so that the strength and violent operacion of
them is mynyshed, by long taryaunce and setlynge. And yet is not their whole
virtue distroyd, but their operacio^ is better and helth^uller.

Against the chopping or ruptures.
The Causes
Much going in cold wyndes and dryness.

The signs need no declaracyo^.

Remedies. Capi. liiii.
HEmlocke leaves stamped and oryed and so made in a plaster, heal all ruptures
or choppynges within.ix or.x. days.

English Galangale healethe the choppynges and deep wounds.

Lyuerworte stampte and drunk with wine, every day is helthfull and good.

Young Hares dressed and orderid with honey in manner of Pylles, and so ministrid,
do close up and make hole choppes and ruptu^es.

Item hares dounge myxt with Honey and given often unto the pacyent to drink,
in the bigness of a bean closes up the ruptures mightylye.

Let the head of a got be sodden hear and al, y^ in water of a gourd, and
eat the meat thereof, or drink the water, it makes all the inward parts of
a man hole and sound.

Of the Agew called ephimera which endures but one day.
The Causes.
The vital spirits in a wonderful unnatural heat without putretactyon,
which comes of much watching, sadness, anger, ho^ger, or dronkenesse.

The Signs.
Great heat in the body with a fever and ending in a sweat or vapor.

Remedies. Capi. lv.
First make a syrup of the decoction of saunders, and the flowers of water
Lylyes, then let the pacyent avoid and eschew all things that burn the
heart* and all that are gross and hot, and if ye vital spirits be in flamid
cheflye above all things bring the pacient in a soft sleep, and let him
smell to Camfore with rose water, and violettes and such like, and minister
things that cause coldn^s and comfort the heart, as Margarites, and sanders,
and the scrapynge of Iuorye, or let him be anoyntid with oil of Rosis and
Nenufar, upon the breast and plasture thereon cold things te^perid with Uenyger,
and it is very good against the heat: if ye natural spirits be inflamid, take
cold syrops and electuaryes that cause coldness, as are sugar, Rosys, and
Uiolettes and plaster the rosys and sau^ders upon the liver, but if it be of a
cold cause beware of letting of blood, to engender more cold the^by and
specially if it be with a rewme.

Give unto the pacyent rose water newlye made myxt with sugar or violettes, and
let him smell to basyl, yet let him not smell to other sweet sauoures, yt be
hot, and in a hot rewmatike cause, let him use a cold fomentatyon and
ointment, but chefelye if it come of over much labor, or copulacion or heat
of ye air and such like, let the holownes of the hands and the souls of the
fete be anoyntid with oil of Uyolettes rosys woman's milk, also anoynte the
back bone, the forehead and temples with oil of rosys, Populion, woman's milk
that gives a woman child suck, and let his meat and drink be of light
dygestyon, and cold, but if it be of over much labor or of over much emptines
he must be nouryshed with resumptiues and confortatyues, if he cannot sweet,
this will heat him incontine^t and mynister occasion unto the pacient to sweet.

Let the leaves of Sallowe tree and Holyhoke, Uiolettes and rosis, and such
like boil together in water, wherein put a great clothe, and let ye pacyent be
wrappyd in the same being warm and coueryd therwyth till he sweet, and
afterward let him wash his feet arms legs in the same decoctyon.

Item the joyce of Cucumers with oil of rosys anoyntid upon ye pulsys and upon
the heart, Dyosco.
asswagethe the heat of the Ague.

Platearius had a certain pacie^t destytute of strength, and put him in a
bathe of water, wherein sodden Eggs were resoluid and after the bathing he
departed strong.

Put a grene Gourde in paste, and bake it in an oven, and afterwrynge out the
joyce and put it into a pot and sethe therein Hens flesh or of some other bird
(first well washte with wine and salt) and a few graynes of whete and Barlye
Lycorice, gume, of Arabike, drago^s Rosys, flowers of water Lylys, fleworte,
Almondes, of the gume of ye Almound tree, Basil* Reasons, myrabolans, Sebesten
sede, the seeds of a gourd, Mellon and Cucumer being al clean dressed put the^ in
a pot well closyd with claye, and let them boil till the third part be washid
afterward strain it and put sugar to the strayner and make a syrup thereof
and give it unto the pacient, it restores very well, and temperatelye colythe
and helthfullye comfortithe fayntinge persons.

Of a contynual Agew.
The Causes.
Abundance of putrefyed humors contained within the veins.

The Signs.
Contynuall heat and pains unto the end of the Fever,

Remedies. Capi. lvi.

colethe, and intolerable heat of sharp agewes.

Of the tertian Fever.
The Causes.
Much choleric humor putrefyeng in the sensible parts of the body.

The Signs.
To have a fyt every other day and not to endure above.xii. hours.

of digestio^, he shall have the Agewe no more.

lesser nettel that grows in a very dry and warm place stamped with much
salt, for shortly after the Fever shall cease.

against al kind of Tertian fevers.

Putrefyed phlegm driven by nature to all the sensible parts of the body.

Of a Quartane Fever.
The Causes.
Melancholy putrefyed having recourse to diverse parts of man.

The Signs.
To have two good days and the thryd a sore fyt.

For a Carbuncle and venomous bytyng.
The Causes
Gross and hot blood having recourse to any one place.

The Signs.
A sore and paynfull ulcer or byle with a foul scabbe as it were brennyd with

stinging, and other of her ki^d and therefore it is a wounderfull remedy.

Cressys stampte and mynglid with branne healyth the carbuncle plasteryd thereon.

The ordure of a man is very good often times before brekyng forth and after.

Against a hollow ulcer or fistula.
The Causes.
A corrupt and sharp humor in any membre.

The Signs.
A deep holow ulcer narow and hard with al.

that groeth in meadows, ye tender stalks of docke, and Betony make the^ al to

morning nountide and night, it is sovereign and heals al kinds of fistules
and holow ulcers if they be curable if not the pacient shall vomit it up again.

Powder made of a bogges head healith the fistule, the cancre, and al
fylthynes in holow ulcers.

To heal an old Leprye. Auycen
Take a serpent of a dry hyl, and cut of the head thereof quickly, and the

and cause the pacient to eat thereof every day. i. and drink ye wine where in
the serpent has been sodden, till the leprouse person be swollen and puffed up

pacient in a stewe or hot house, and let the hole body of the pacient be

flesh and skin is thereby renuid, and so shall the pacient be perfytly healid.

of honey every day.

and drink the water where in they were sodden and let him wash his hands, face,
and berd therewith.

draw broken bones out from ulcers.

A drink for them that be hurt and bruysed. Remedies. Ca. lxix.
^^len.
FOr them that be bruysid, take Betonye, Egrimony, Strawbery leaves, Azarabacca
or fool foot, malowes* buglosse, ta^sy, margeram, Five leaued grass, Saynct
John's grass, and Pimpernell gather of each.M.i. stamp them and sethe them
with.iii. pound of wine and the same wine yt remanith strain, and put thereto an
hundredth corns of peper, and the oftener that the pacient drinks thereof, the
sooner shall he be whole, but let him beware from all poisoned and hurtful
things.

Incorporate the powder of fragra^tcense and whet branne with percely joyce
that they may be good and thick, and so apply the same to ye sore.

Take a gober of larde, and take honey branne and Fenigreke and wine sethe them
all together, and apply it upon ye sore of the strippe, it wou^derfully
helpith and healith.

A drink that is wounderfull against bruysing.

Take Egrimony, betony, Sage, Plantayne, Iuy leaves, rospercely poune them
together and myxte wine thereto, give the pacient it often to drink till he be
whole.

To cure beasts that are sick or hurt.
THe blood of a graye myxt with salt and instilled into the horns of beasts
preserves the^ from the moren this is well known and prouyd

with vinegar, takes away the hurt of them.

Peter. Lu.
Cut the beast and put into the wou^d powder of black Hellebore which with his
property draws out poisoned humors, and so the beast shall be delivered from
the moren.

If the beast drink a good hearty draught of ynke it will heal it.

Against dronkennes. Cap. lxxi.
Give unto that man that is given to dronkennes the lights of a sheep, and he
shall feel no dronkennes.

Give unto a dronken man the ashes of burnt swalows, and he shall not be drunk
while he lives.

the rote of mugwort, and so shall his werynes depart from him.

To pourge the choleric humor down ward. Capi. lxxv.
TO purge Colericke humors downward by the bellye, and that in helthful men:
first let the matter be digestid, with Oxizaccharum, or else with sirupus
Acetosus, the matter being digestid, pourge it with this medicine. Take of ye
electuari desuccorosatu^ oximel, resoluid with the joyce of rosis ana. ii. of ye
joyce of scamoni. and a half mingle the^ together and if you will you may give
ye pacie^t thereof tempered with wine or you may make thereof pills.

If it so chance that the matter be contained from the navel downward or in
any other part of the body, then myngle with the fore rehersyd medicines. ii.
of the powder of mirabolanes citrines, of all this make pills, and let them be
given to ye pacient.

Of Melancholy natural. Capi. lxxvi.
TO purge natural mela^cholie in helthful men, fallen in the nether parts of
ye body, first digest ye matter with squillitike oximel, or else with some syroupe
made therefore, ye matter being digestid purge it with this medicine.

Take of Hierologodion. ii. of hiera rufi. i. of theodoricon emp. i. of honye
Anacardine.. mengle them together and make pills, and give it in the euenning
and let them be sharpenyd with. i. of spurge.

If the matter which ought to be purged, be in the middell parts of the bodi,
as in the stomach, or in the inward of man thereunto must be aplyed laxatiues,
as Cassia fistula. and.c. or as the medicine above mencionid.

But if it be inseueral parts of the body as in the gout in such a case must
strong medicines be ministrid as is rehearsal of before, and they ought to be
doubled.

Of purging burnt collar. Capi. lxxvii.

with this medicine. Take Catar: Imperial, oximel laxatiue, of each. ii. of
Hierologodian. i. of spurge. i. mengle them together and make pills give them
in the euenyng.

The aphorisms of Hippocrates redacted unto a certain order, according unto
y^ members of a man's body, and the dyseases that may fall in any of them.
Of the disposityon of the head. Capi. prim.
VRyne troubled like unto the water of an Ox or horse signifies pains in the
head.

Milk is evil for them that have the head ache,

If y^ pains be in ye nodle of ye head it is good to cut ye vain in ye forhed

If any matter or water flow out at his nose or ears which has the head
ache, it takes away ye pains.

Whatsoever helthful man is suddenly payned in the head and therewith losyth his
voice and routeth withal, he dies within seven days, if an Agew take him not.

Of the lethargye or forgetfulness. Capi. ii.
To tremble in a lythargy is very evil.

Of the pain in the head called subeth. Ca. iii.
IN this disease paynfull sleep is mortal.

Of to much watchynge. Cap. iiii.
Immoderat sleep or watching is very evil.

Of the Palsy. Capi. v.
PAlseys do commenly chance from xl. years of age till.lx

It is hard to help a small palsy, but to heal a greuouse palsy it is
ympossible.

It is no matter what kind of spume or froth be about their mouths which be
strangled or have thhe palsy, and be not yet dead.

Of the madness called melancholia. Capi. vi.
A Swellynge or weakness endurynge a long time brings a ma^to a melancholy.

Peryllouse eruptons in all melancholyke dyseases, do signifye either the palsy
a conuulsyon, blyndenesse or madn^sse.

The Hemorrhoydes be very good to such as be melancholyke.

Of Ragyng madness. Capi. vii.
IF he that is mad be taken with a laxe or hidropsye, it is good

The Hemorrhoydes breaking out, take a way madness.

If a mad man use to laughe it is a laudable sign, but if he be very sad, it
is peryllouse.

If a mad man find ease in sleaping it is good, but if his rage increase, it
is to be fearyd.

Of the falling Evil. Capi. viii.
They which have the falling evil in their childhod be often healed, but if they
be past.xxv. year old, they die for the most part.

The changing of place time, and age curethe the falling evil in young men.

Of the diseases in the synowes. Ca. ix
ALl cold things be noyouse to the synowes, the bones, ye teth the brains and
the mary in the back, and unto those al hot things be profitable and good.

A sodeyne Fever heals y^ cra^pe.

A convulsyon after sleep in an ague, is to be feared.

To be short breathyd in an ague is the sign of a convulsion.

A convulsyon or gripinges in the belly in sharp agues, be very evil.

A convulsyon after the drynking of hellebore, is deadly.

To have a convulsyon with a sore wound is death.

A conuulsyon is perillouse to him that has blede much.

A convulsyon or yeskynge after a great inadityon be very evil.

If a dronken man lose his speech and have a co^uulsyo^ he shall shortly die.

A convulsion comes of immoderate fullness or emptiness and so does yeskynge.

Yeskinge, vomiting, a convulsio^ or m^dnesse coming upon him yt is payn^d in
the small guts are, to be fearyd.

The crampe or madness with much watching, is very perillouse.

He that is taken with a sore convulsyon if he live four days shall e^kape.

A convulsyon after a purgatyon is very perillouse.

If a young man being fleshy be taken with a distension of the synowes in the
Somer time. let him be washed with cold water for ye does increase the heat,
and ye heat does assuage his pains.

In sore wounds a convulsion or distencyon be very evil.

Of the drousynes in the head. Capi. ^.
TO dote or to be astonished after a blow or stripe is, very evil,

Of the members being set awrye. Capi. xi.
IN a contynuall agew if the lyppes, the eyes, the brows or the nose stand
awry, so that the pacyent can not hear or see and be therewith very weke, he
shall dye shortly after.

Of the disposicion of the eyes. Capi. xii.
OF the times of ye year if it chance the winter to be dry and ye northwind to
blow, the springtime moist with the southwynd, ye somer following there shall
many be troubled with blernesse, but of the contrary part if the winter be
moist with much southwind, and the springtime dry with northwindes, men
shall be likewise vexed with dry blernisse.

If in autune, or Heruest there be much drought, and northwyndes, it shall do
good to moist persons and women, but other it shall vex with dry blernes.

When the times of the year be dry many shall have bler eyes.

The southwynde blowinge daily for a season, will engender daselinge in the eyes.

Diseases of the eyes do cheflye rainge in somer.

In a continual agewe, if the eyes be wrythen a side, and the pacyent weak
and cannot see, it is a pr^sent token of death.

In all kinds of Fevers, and other diseases, voluntarye tears be laudable*
but if they flow contrary to the pacyentes mind, they be to be fearyd.

It is very good* if he that is diseasyd in ye eyes be taken with a sode^ lax.

All dyseasys in the eyes be healyd either by drinking of sweet wynes, or with
baths of whote water or lettyng of blood or with a purgacio^.

If a man be seek mark his eyes when he slepyth for if any white thing
appear betwixt the eye liddes, and the pacient have no great laxe nor
received any purgatio^ before, is a terrible and deadly sign.

Of the disposion of the ears. Capi. xiii.
Whosoever uses to void choler, and in ye mean while waxes defe, the laxe
stops, and of the contrary part, a sodeyne lax and deiectyon of choler
takes away defnesse.

To wax defe in a continual agew (the pacyent being weak of body) is a
token of death.

Uoluntary bleding at the nose or a sudden lax does take away the de^nes
which comyth of an ague.

Of the dysposition of the nose. Capi. xiiii.
THey whose nostrilles be full of superfluouse moystnesse, and have also their
nature or seade very watrish, be not helthful of body, and they that be
contrary enjoy continual health.

Horsnesse and continual fluxion of sneuil in old men, do in no mea^s wax
ripe.

A dry Somer with often northwynd and a moist Harvest with ye southwind, does
engendre in ye next winter the head ache, ye coughe horsenesse, and much
fluxyon of rewme by the nosthrils, but if the Heruest be dry and the northwynd
blow, the rewme shall endure much longer. Old men be often greuyd with
fluxyon of rewme and ye coughe.

Much rewme contained in the stomach is changed within twenty days to plain
matter.

All cold things as snow and yse, do engender distillatyons.

Of the bledinge at the nose. Capi. xv.
OLd men and children do often blede at the nose.

If it chance him that is seek of an agewe to blede, he shall have a laxe in
the decrease of his fever.

He that waxes deffe through an agewe and bledithe at the nose shall recover
his hearing.

Who so is like to have an apostem in any of his joints and in the mean while
bleadeth at the nose is sure to recover his health.

If a woman whose flowers be stopped do chance to blead at the nose it is a
good sign.

Bleding at the nose or ears takes away the headake.

To have the crampe or to dote while the nose bledeth is an evil sign.

Of nesing. Capi xvi
IF a woman having the mother, or being in pains of child birth, chance to
nese. it is very good.

Nesinge takes away belchinge.

All nesing that comes of the head is caused either of the brain being hot,
or the empti place of the head being very moist, for the air with in
contained brekith out through a narowe passage, and thereby causes the noise.

Of the disposions of the mouth and tongue. Capi. xvii.
Young children and infantes be often troubled with ulcers in the mouth, and
to much vomytinge.

Of al other men they which lispe, be most troubled with mani sieges, and laxes.

Of the diseases in the teth. Capi. xviii.
IT is the sign of contynuance in an ague, to have much slimy matter about the
tethe.

When the teeth begin to grow children are payned with fevers, crampes, and
ytchinge of the gummes* and espicially in the growyng of the gu^me teethe.

Of the grefes in the throat. Ca. xix
OFtentimes diseases propre for the somer season do chance in autumn, as the
squinancy, shortness of breath, and the pains in the flape that covers the
wind pype.

A suffocatyon chancinge to him that has an agew, and no swelling remain in
the throat, is a token of death.

If the squinancye fall down to the lyghtes, and the pacient live seven days,
the fluxion will turn to matter

If he that has the squinancy do swell in the neckei, it is a good token for the
fluxion is driven outward.

He that has an agew not being able to turn his neck, neither to swallowe
his meat, without a manifest swelling in the throat, shall short lie dye.

Of the breast and lyghtes. Cap. xx.
TO have the brethe somewhat stopped in an agew is an evil token, for a
convulsyon shall shortly follow, they which have swellyng in their backs before
they be xiiii. year old coming of shortness of brethe, or a sore cough, shall
shortly dye.

If it chance a dro^ken man suddenly to fall spechlesse, he shall shortly dye of
a conuulsyon, except either he fall to an agew, or else he receive his spech
again at the hour when the surfyt is digestyd.

They which suddenly ar taken with pains in the head, and therwyth lose their
speech and route, they dye shortly, if they be not taken with an agew. Whosoever
has his brains hurt any way, does suddenly lose his spech.

Of blood spyttynge. Capi. xxi.
Young men be chieflye troubled with spittyng of blood, consumptyons, hot
fevers, and the falling Evil.

The spyttel in a continual Fever being wane of color, bloody, stinkyng, or
choleric, is an euel toke^.

He that spitteth frothy blood is diseasyd in the lyghtes.

If he that spitteth blood, spit therewith al filthye matter, it is an evil
sign.

To vomit blood without an agew is helthful, but in an ague peruicious

Of the pleurisye. Capi. xxii,
IF in the beginning of a Pleurysye the pacyent use to spit, it shortneth the
disease, but if it chance afward it prolongeth the pains.

The Northwynd blowing a long season to geder, engenders colykes coughes, and
pleurisyes.

Pleurisyes, peripeunomyes, rewmes, and coughes do chiefli raygne in the winter.

If he which has the pleurisy, be not purged in.xiiii. days, the fluxyon
will change to matter.

The pleurisy once changed to matter, if the pacie^t be not purged with in
forty days after the brekinge forth of the matter, he shall fall to a
consumptyon.

A sodeyne laxe following a pleurysie or a peripeunomy, is very peryllouse.

They whose belchinge smellith ^umwhat sharp or tarte, be not given to the
pleurisye.

The frenesye in a peripeunomye is an evil token.

Whosoever having filthy matter in the void place of the stomach, or having
the hydropsy, is la^ced or bre^ned, if all the matter or water issue furthe, it
is present death.

Of the consumpsion or ptisike. Cap. xxiii
Autumn or heruest is very yuill to the^ which be in a consumption.

A dry somer with much northewynd, and a moist heruest with southwyndes, do
engendre in the winter following coughes and rewmes, and to diverse,
consumptyons.

In consumptions purge downward, and upward.

They which be betwixt.xviii. and.xxv. be chieflye troubled with the ptisike.

If his spittell which has a consumpsition being cast upon coals do stincke,
and the hear fall of his head, it is a sign of death.

A sodeyne laxe to him that is in a consumptyon and his hear fall o^ is deadly.

Milk is unwholesome to the^ which have the headake, or that be syke of any
fever, and to the^ which hau^ noise and wind in the hyer part of there belyes,
and that have cholerike decoctions in hot fevers, or yt have lost much of
their blood, and of the contrary part, it is good to such as have a
consumption without an agew, and also it may be ministered to them which have
agewes long time, if none of the abouesayd tokens do appear, and to such as
have been long seek of a consumption.

Aptisike or laxe with spittynge of fylthy matter if the spittinge cease is
deadly.

Of the dispositions of the heart Ca. 24.
GReat brennynge in the stomach and prickynge about the h^rt is an evil token
in an agew.

They which lose their strength of ^entymes without manifest occasion shall dye
suddenly.

Of the Pappes. Capi. xxv.
IF the Pappes of a woman which is with child of two do wax lyttel, ^he shall
lose one child, and if it be ye right Pappe it is a man child, and if it be
the lift a woman.

If a woman, that neither is with child, another has brought furthe a child,
have milk in her pappes, she is past her Flowers.

Blood drawing to the pappes of a woman, is a sign of the frenesy.

If thou will stop the flowers of a woman, put a great ventose upon her
pappes.

Much milk yssuyng out of the tetes of a woman yt is with child, betokens
the child to be very weak and feeble, but if the pappes be hard the child is
strong and helthful.

Like as the decreasing of the pappes is a sign of the destructyon of the
child, so the hardness of the same signifies great pains, in the pappes,
legs, knees, or eyes, and the life of the child.

Of the stomach. Cap. xxvi.
THe stomach is most hot in the winter and springtyme and then also the
slepes be longest.

Men can not well away with much meat in the somer and herueste, but meanly in the
spring, and best of all in the winter.

In all dyseases to be steadfast of mind, and to be content with such things as
be mynystred to him, is a laudable sign, but the contrary is very evil.

Drink of wine does take away hunger.

If he which goes very dry to bed step, it is good.

If they which have certain murmuryng and wynd in their belyes, have great
pains in the loins, they shall have moist deiections, if ye wind do nether com
forth nor great multitude of vryne, and al these do chance in fevers.

If in a laxe or vomit such things be purged as ought to be purged, it does
ease the pacie^t and it is nothing greuouse, but if no it chau^ceth contrary.

Let such as can not easly vomit, be purged downewarde, but not in the somer.

In all kind of diseases if black choler be purged upward or downewarde
without a medicyne, it is perillouse.

In the pains of the small guts called yl^aca, vomytynge, yeskynge,
convulsyon, or dotynge be evil.

A convulsion and yeskyng after a great purging, ar to be fearyd.

A sodeyne and voluntary vomiting, heals him that has had a long laxe.

Yeskynge is good to him which has a heat and swelling in the liver.

Of the diseasys in the liver. Capi. xxvii
AN agew takes away ye grefe and pains in the liver.

A wound in the brains, heart, midrife, small guts, stomach, or liver is
deadly.

If he whose liver mattreth be bre^nid and therout issue pure and whit matter,
he shall eskape, but if it be lik dregs he shall shortly dye.

Many diseases proper, to ye somer do chance in harvest, as quartaines and
Hydropsyes engendryd in the spleen.

If he which has the dropsye be woundyd, it is hard to hele him. Whosoever
has grypinges about the hauel, and pains in the loins and cannot be helped
by purgatio^s or otherwise shall fall to a dry hidropsye.

The coughe goinge before the hidropsye is evil, but in the hydropsy much worse.

If they which he splenetike, have a blody flux which will long continewe, they
fall to the hydropsye, or their meat shall cume through the^ vndygestyd and so
they dye.

A bloody flux, an hidropsy or madness after a frenesy, are laudable.

Whosoever have their liver full of water, and it break downwarde to the belly, it
is death.

If he that has an agew be taken wi^h the yelow iandes ye.vii. the.ix. the.xi.
or.xiiii. day, it is laudable, if the right side wax not hard, but if it do,
it is contrary.

An agew takes away the pains under the syddes, if it be without great heat
and swellyng.

Of the gaul and spleen. Capi. xxviii.
IF the yelow Iaundes, chance in an agew before the seventh day, it is evil.

They which have the yelow iandes be not full of wynd.

If there liver which have the yelowe ye iandes be hard, it is an evil sign.

A bloody flux is good to th^^ y^ be splenetyke.

Of al kind of fluxyons. Cap. x^^^
IN a laxe diverse kinds of (...) be good, except they change to (...) as be
evil.

Black sieges like to fylthy b^^ude being voluntary be wounder^^^l evil
wh^rther they be with an (...) or without an agew, and ye de^ker to our they have,
the worse they be, but if these sieges com through a p^rgacion they be more
laudable, (...) and although they be of diverse colors the be not evil.

To have a siege of plain m^^^^cholye, or to perbreake the same in y^
beginning of any disease is deadly

Whosoever is brought weak either by some greuouse disease or siknes of long
contynua^ce, or by wou^des received, or any other way, and thereupon have a
syege of melancholy like to black blood he shall doutlesse dey the day after.

A bloody flux beginning with a melancholic siege, is deadly.

Little peaces ^f flesh appearinge in a bloudye sie^e, be tokens of present
death.

Uayne desire to the stole in a woman with child, kills the child.

Tart or sharp belching suddenly chancing to him whose meat comes through
him indigestid, is very good.

In long continuance of a bloudye flux, to abstain from meat, is very evil
and if it be with an ague much wors

A bloody flux is good to such as be splenetike.

A sudden bloody flux after a sincer or clean siege, is to be fearyd.

If a great laxe chance in a white morfewe, it takes away ye disease.

Frothy sieges in a flux, do declare the phlegm to come from the head.

It is an evil token in a sharp agewe, to have a convulsion, or painful
gripinges in the belly.

Pains in the hyer parts of the belly, be more gentle and of leasser peril
then they which be in the lower part.

If he which has the strangurye, be taken with the pains in the small guts
called iliaca, he shall dye with in seven days, except a fever take him with
much flux of vryn.

Of the fundament. Ca. xxx.
IF the Hemorrhoydes chance to such as be melancolike mad, or frentike, it is
laudable.

If he that has long time had the hemorrhoydes be healyd, and not one left
open, it is to be feared least he fall to a consumptyon or hidropsye

The hemorrhoydes be very good to such as have a mela^cholike madness, or
great grefe in the raynes.

Of the disposicyon of raynes. Capi. xxxi.
THey which have the pains in the raynes after.xl. years of age, can not be
healyd.

They whose vryne is full of grauel be seek of the stone, either in the raynes,
or in the bladder.

Dyseases in the raynes and bladder, are skant curable in old men. Little
bladders or bubles in a ma^s vryne, do betoken pains in the raynes, and long
diseasys.

The hyer part of the vryne fattye and thick, is a sign of pains in the
raynes and sum greuouse disease.

If the above said tokens appear in such as be seek in the raynes, and also
have sore pains in the muscles of ye back, if the pains be inward it
signifies an apostem in the inner parts, but if they be outward the apostem
shall be there also.

Much phlegm contained betwixt the stomach and the midrife, having no way to
the belly, is sone dissoluid if it issue by the veins to the bladder, and
thence forth in vryne.

Of the diseases in the bladder. Cap. 32.
IN moist and wete season, long agewes fluxes, rottenesse, ye falling evil,
the squinancy, and the palsye do cheflye raygne, but contrary in dry seasons,
co^sumptions, blearnes goutes, stra^guryes and bloody fluxes

Children be often grieved with pains in the throat, and fallinge of the jaws,
worms in the belly, and stranguryes.

Old men have most comenlye these diseasys, shortness of brethe, rewme, the
coughe, the stra^guri, difficulty of vryne, goutes, daselinge in the head,
pains in ye raynes, palses in their bodies out of just temperanse, y^ ytche,
watchinges with moystnesse in the belly eyes and nosthriles dullness of sight, and
hering.

If his water that is seek of an Ague be litell in quantity thick and full of
cru^mes, and th^rvpo^ his vryne follow much in quantity and thine it is very
good,

Whosoever in an ague has his water troubled like to the vryne of an ox or
cow, has or shortly shall have the headake.

In such diseasys as shall be endyd the seventh day, there shall appear in the
pacyentes vryne a red cloud the fourth day with other reasonable tokens.

Uryne white and clear is not laudable, and especially in them which be
frentike or do^ing.

They which be like to have an apostem in their joints, be deliuerid thereof by
much vryne white and thick as that which comes from such as have been iiii.
days seek of an ague

Blood or matter in the urine does declare ulcers, and biles, either in ye
raynes or blad^er.

Little pieces (...) flesh and hears in the vryne co^^ from the raynes.

Contents lyk^ branne in ye urine signifye a Pocke or Scabbe in the bladder.

They which p^sse blood have a vain broken in the ^^ynes.

If they which (...) blood or cromes, or else hau^ ^he ^tranguri, if the pains
be bene^h the beli about the share, the disease is in the bladder.

Gravel in the vryne betokens ye stone in the bladder.

He that pisseth blood or matter, and he in whose urine skales do appear, or
the water have a strong smell, has ulcers in the bladder.

Whosoever has pustules or welkes in his yard, and if they break and the matter
run out, they shall be shortly hole.

To piss much in the night, does betoken a lytlel siege.

The strangury chances to that parson which has a hot swellinge in the
fundament, or matrix, and to him whose reins do matter, and yesking ever
follows the heat and swellyng in the liver.

Diseases in the raynes and blader, are hard to heal in old men.

Conte^tes in the botome of the urine like unto thick branne, signify the
disease long to continue.

If the water do appear unlike of substance, it betokens great
mystempera^ce, for diuersitye of humors within the body.

Drinking of wine, heals ye stra^gurye, and him yt cannot hold his water,
and it is also good to let blood of the inner veins about ye ancle.

Of the membr^s of generatyon in men. Capi. xxxiii.
Likewise in men, either for the raritie of the body, the spirits goo out, so
that the seed ca^ not come to his due place: or for the thiknesse thereof the
humor cannot get furthe, neither wax hot for the coldness, and so it heapeth
in yt place or else ye same thing comes of great heat.

A bone a gristel, a synow, and the the top of the yard being cut, will
nether grow nor join together.

Of the members of generation in women. Ca. xxxiiii
IF the winter be moist and warm and the southwind blow, the spri^g time dry
with northwyndes, those women that be then with child shall of every light
occasyon lose their children, and the children then borne shall be weak and
seckely, wherefore they shall either dye strenght with, or else al their life time
be, fayntye and full of diseasys.

If a woman with child must ned^ be purged, let that be from ye fourth month
to the seventh, yet those su^what leasse, but before four and after seuin let
the^ receive no purgacions

The suffumigation of sweet odurs does bring forth the flowers, and is good for
diverse other things if it did not cause ye head to be drousi.

Lettynge of blood does kill the child, but the nyer ye birth the more
perillouse it is.

If a woman with child be taken with any greuouse disease, it is death.

The fluxyon of the flowers takes a way vomiting of blood.

If the flowers stop it is good to blede at the nose.

It is perillouse for a woman with child to have a great laxe.

Nesynge is very good to her that has the mother, or that trauaylethe of
childbyrth.

She whose flours be evil colourid or that keep not their common cour^^ had need
to take a purgatyon.

If thou would know whether ^ woman has conceyuyd or no, geu^ her water and
honey myngled together to drink when she goes to sleep and if she feel
grypinges and pains in her belie she is with child, i^ she feel non she is
not.

A woman which has conceuyd a male is well colouryd, but if it be a female,
it is contrary.

Those women which be very small and lean before they conceive, shall lose one
child before they wax gross, Those women which being mean of body, do lose
their children the second or third month without manifest occasyon, have the
closures of their wombes full of fylthy matter, wherefore they cannot sustain
the weight of ye child, but suddenly break.

They which be very fat cannot conceive till they wax lean, for the ^outh of
their matrix is stopped ^p with fatness.

If thou wylt provoke the flowers ^ause the woman to nese, and in the ^eane
while stop her nose and mouth

They which be with child have ^heyr wombes closed up.

If a woman with child be taken with an agew, and wax very hot, without
manifest occasion, she has great pains in childebyrthe, or else ^he loses her
child with peril of her ^wne life.

If a convulsyon, and faintness ^ake a woman in ye time of her flou^^s, it is
perillouse.

If the flowers have to much issue there do ensue diverse diseases, and if they
be stopped there follows great grefe in the womb.

If a woman has not conceived, and thou will know whether she shall conceive or
no* let her be well coueryd with clothes, and beneth let a suffumigacion be
made of hot things and odoriferous, for if the smell com up through her body
to the nose and mouth, be sure yt she is not barayne of her self.

If a woman with child have her flours, it is impossible ye child should be
helthfull.

The flowers stopping with an ague or great cold, and the woman loathe her meat,
say she is with child.

The matrix cold and gross, or very moist, is not apt to conceive, for ye seed
is therein quenched and distroyed. Likewise if it be dry and very hot, for the^
is the seed lost for lack nourishment, but they whose matrix is of a mean
temperature be ple^tifull and do often conceive, if you wilt know more read
above in ye disposion of ye Pappes.

Of the disposyon of the outward members Capi. xxxv.
IF two great grefes do happen in diverse me^bres at one time, the gre^ter
takes away the leasse.

Pains in the knees and loins, or grypynges in the belly coming upon him that
has non agew, do sygnifye that he should be purged down ward.

In paynful fevers apostemes do often happen about the knees and chekes.

The sickness shall chiefly remain in that place which was greuyd before it
began.

The joints of such as have had a fever for a long season, shall ache and be full
of pustules.

Great pains and swellynges in the joints with any brekinge or issue, do
signify that the gout or cra^pe shall follow, and many be remedied with much
washyng with cold water, for yt does extenuat the humor and take a way the
pains, for a mean cold extinguisheth.

Letting of blood does utterly take a way such pains as begin at ye back,
and thence remove to the arms. Enuches be never bald nor gouty.

Women have never the gout as long as they have their flowers.

A child has never the gout until he has known a woman.

All kind of goutes (if the infla^mation be quenchid) within forty days, do
end.

All goutes do chieflye reygne in springtyme and harvest.

If the hippe bone fall out of his place after a long sciatica, there shall
much matter follow, or the leg will consume away, and the pacient shall
halt, except he be brennyd.

Of the Fevers and Agues. Capi. xxxvi.
THe sickness it self, and the time of ye year do plainly declare the time of
the fyttes, the chief time of the disease, and the order in y^ fittes.

Old men be never troubled with (...) sore agewes because their bodies be cold.

All sharp diseasys are judged in fourtene days.

Quartanes in somer be very short in Autumn much longer, in winter longest of
all.

It is much better that he which has a convulsyon be taken with an agew,
then he which has an agewe be taken with a convulsyon.

If his flesh that has a sore ague do either fall nothing away at al or
decay very much it is evil for the first betokenith long contynuance of the
disease, and the other great wekenesse in the person.

At the beginning and ending of an agew, al things be of more stre^gthe then
in the chief part thereof.

In all diseases they be in leasse ieopardy to whose nature age, accusto^, or
time of the year the sickness does agree, then they with whom it does in no
point agree.

When the somer is not unlike to the spring time you shall look for much
sweting in all agewes.

In dry seasons there shall reygne diverse sore agewes.

All dyseases in the harvest season be perillouse and deadlye, but in the
springtyme most gentyl and easy.

In the somer these do chiefly reygne, contynual and brenynge agews tertyan and
quartayne fevers, vomyting, laxes, blernesse with ulcers in the mouth and
pryuy members. A cold stiffness chanci^g the sixth day in any fever does take
away all iudgmente.

All fevers which do not intermite and give over the third day be perillouse,
but if the paciente have no fyte that day there is no ieope^dy.

If great coldness take him which is very weke through a contynuall agew it is
deadly.

If in a contynuall agew the outward members be very cold and the inward
parts hot and dry, it is a token of death

If in an agew pustules and pains chance in the joints, it is a sign that
the pacient fedeth well.

In a contynuall Fever, if the lyppes, the eyes, the Nose or the mouth be
wrythen and out of fashyon, so that the pacient can not se nor here and
therewith all his body be weak, it is a sign that death is at hand.

A sodeyne laxe or dotage in a continual fever is deadly.

An apostem which does not break at the first iudginge day in a Fever, does
signify the long contynuance of the disease.

Uoluntary tears in agewes be laudable, but they which flow against the
pacyentes will be to be fearyd.

Al Agewes with swellinge in the foundament be evil except such as endure but
one day.

If he which has an agew do sweat very much and the disease contynew it is
evil, for it betokens long syknesse and abundance of humors

He that has a convulsyon or discencion in ye synowes, and thervpo^ an agew,
is suddenly delivered.

A tertyan not endid in seven fittes shall continue long.

The yelowe iaundes coming upon him that has a Fever before the seventh day is
perillouse.

To be affrayde in his sleep, or to have the cramp is evil.

To be short brethyd in an agew is the sign of a convulsyon.

Soryful syghes in sharp agewes be to be fearyd.

They which have the quartaine have seldom convulsyons, and if he which has a
convulsion fall to a quartayne he shall be deliuerid from his conuulsyon.

If he which has an agew swette in these days following it is very good, the
third, the.v.vii, ix.xi.xiiii.xvii.xxi*xxvii, xxxi.xxxiiii. for ye swetes do
judge ye fever, but if they be otherwise, they declare long contynuance of ye
disease and great pains.

Of the diete to be observed in agues. Capi. xxxvii
IN all diseases of long continuance the pacyent most use little meat, and
exquisite, but in sharp diseasis yt is perillouse, yet to eat to little or to
much be both evil.

Secke m^n do more often err in using little meat, then in that diet which
is sumwhat larger, whereby they be often hurt, yea and to such as be in health
small fare, and exquisite diete, is very perillouse, because they easly err
therein.

Unto extreme diseases extreme cures be necessary.

When the disease is most extreme and sharp the pacyent shall by and by have
wonderful pains, wherefore he most use most small and thin diet and as the
disease is from extreme pains so most the diet amend.

When ye seknesse is most vyole^t then most the pacie^t use least meat of al.

The physician most mark well whyther the pacyent using such small diet may
endure to the state and strength of the disease, or whyther the pains will
first assuage or no

If the sickness in the beginnynge be most fervent, then most the pacicyent use
little meat, but if the siknes be afterward most vyolent the pacyentes meat
most be sumwhat before diminished, but in the beginning he most feed well that
he may be able to abide the disease.

The pacyent most forbear meat in the fyttes, and especially in such agewes
yt do intermyt and come bifits. Among al other old me^ may best a way with
fasti^g, the^ such as be of middell age, after young men, and worse of al
children and especially such as be quick and lusty.

Such as grow, have much natural heat within them and therefore do require
much meat, which if they have not their bodies do sone consume, but contrary
litel meat will ^erue old men, because they have but little natural hete which
with much meat is sone quenched, and therefore they have not so fervent Agues
because their bodies be cold.

The stomach and inward parts be most hot in winter and springetime, wherefore
men most then feed better, for ye inward heat the^ being much does require
much meat and for a proof thereof mark ye ages and ye cha^pio^s Moist meats be
best of al to such as be sike of agues, and chiefly to children, and to such as
have be^ acustomed like meats.

You must mark whether you shall give them meat onse or twyse, and to whom
you must give more, to whom less, and su^what you most bear with the time of
the year, the country, the age of the person, and with the accustomed use.

In somer and autumn men may skarce away with much meat, but in the winter
best of all, and mean in the spring.

To such as have their sickness by certain fyttes in order, you shall give
nothing, nether add nor dimynishe before the time of judging.

Here end the Aphorisms of Hyppocrates, set in order for every membre, and
translatyd out of latin into English by Humfre Lloyd.
A Book conteynyng the names of the co^pound medecines, which be good for all
ky^de of dyseases that may chance in any membre of man's body, in readyng of
which book I would the gentle reader should be admonished of one thing, which
is yt I do comenly through all this book use the latin names, and have not
translatyd ye same to ye English tongue, being mouyd thereunto, because that
many of them he such that they cannot be well Englished, and also that the
Apothecaryes which have such medicynes to sell do comenly use the Latyne or
rather Arabike, and Barbarouse terms, and not the English n^mes thereof, upon
which consideracions I thought it best to use the same through all this
present book.
For all diseasys in the head. Capi. i.
THese confections following do not suffer the hears to wax hoar and gray
electuarium de aromatibus, co^fectio alharif, oleu^ costinum and de alchana.

These be very good for all diseases in the brain, the electuarye of Perles,
Triacle dyatessoron and the confection of musk.

These comfort the brain, aromaticum rofarum: maius aromaticum. dyambra, galie
elepha^gine and pillule stomatice.

These purge the brain, the confectyon alphescera, and pillule elephangene,
Oximell squillitike opens ye opilatyon of the brain.

The infusion of hyera heals the melancolike pains of the head.

These be good for the falling evil, confectio de musco, thiriaca diatessaron,
confectio alfescera, syrupus sticados, acetum and oximel squilliticum,
vnguentum de bdellio, oleu^ de cucumere asmino, de lapide gagatis, de piperibus
and philosophoru^. Co^fectio alharif and kebuli co^diti, be very good for all
diseasis in ye senses

These purge ye instruments of ye senses, pillule elephangine stomatiche*
aggregate and pillule lucis maiores and minores.

Hyerapicra purges al cold diseasis of ye head, so does hiera hermetis,
hieralogodio^ rufi, and pillule aggregate

The cold diseases of the head are healyd with the confectyon of water and honey.

These confectyons ensuynge are good for all pains in the head, oximell
squillitike, infusyon of Hyeratrociskes of cr^o: oil Anet, oil of Laurel, of
spiknard, of elder and oil of wild cucumer,

The infusion of hyera clensith the head, so do pillule stomatice and pillule
aggregate maiores.

Hyera hermetis purges the hemicran, and pillule alha^dach an e^playster of
mustard and oil of euforbium heal the same.

The electuary of rosys purgithe the head ache of an hot cause, and so do

Emplastrum diaquilon ripeth all swellynges.

Trifera sarasenica is good for werinesse.

Unguentum alphesericon, oleum de iunipero and de fraximo heals the pains in
the legs.

Confectio de ass and diasulphur be good for bytynges of venemouse beasts.

Emplastrum de fermento draws al fixed things out of ye body. For ye sciatica
take emplastrum andromachi, e^plm sinapis, oleum de piperibus and philosophor.

Anoint thy body with oil of dyl and thou shall sweat, and oil of quinces
does stop the swette.

Pillule aggregate maiores and serapine purge the sciatica.

These purge sharp agues, trifera persica, alxilcostes, co^fectio de dactilis,

These purge al ki^d of agues, pillule aggregate, de rubarbaro de alkakengi,
