A Table containing ye weightes which phisicyons do comenly use, and the
interpretacyon of the names of the compound medicynes herin contained with the
quantity and time yt they ought to be received in.

THe least and first of al weightes (como^ly used among phisicyons) is a barley
corn, and.xx. corns make a scruple, three scrupules make a drachme, eight
drachmes make an ounce, xii. ounces make apou^de. A quarter of pound is three
ounces,

And they be this notid.
A corn. gra. A scruple.) A drachme. An ounce.. A pound li. A quarter. q. A
half. s. A handful. m. Ana. of every one.

All compounde medycynes be either receyuid within the body, or laid to the
same without* and they which be received into ye body be these.

ELectuarium and confectio differ in this alone, that electuariu^ is moist and
made with sugger and honey, and confectio dry made alonly with sugar, and
because they be for diverse diseases theris nooe certain time or measure, for
the receiving of them.

Mixtura is when diverse electuaries or co^fections be mingled together, and is
received.ii. hours be fore meat. Tragea is when diverse pouders be me^gled
together with sugar and they be received a.. at onest with soppes of strong wine.

Conserua and conditu^ be when diverse spyces be mixed with sum sirup and be
come^ly receiuid early and late after the bygnesse of a walnut.

Loath is a medycyne which may be lyked with the tongue, and may be received at
al times in the quantity of a hasel nutte.

Iuleb is a clear potyon made of diverse waters and sugar.

Rob is a joyce made hard and thick with the heat of the son or of ye fire
and is commonly mingled with electuarys, and conserues.

Syrup is a moist medicyne which may be receyuyd earlye or late

Decoctum is a medicine made of rotes leaves, sead and flowers where unto is
added sugger or honey.

Infusio is when diverse medycins be beaten to powder or hole laid to stepe a
certain space in sum liquor

Trochiscus is a round confectio^ and plain, made after the manner of a whele,
the which before it be receiuyd most be beaten to powder, and drunk with wine
or other licoure the weight of one. commonly.

Pills be known to al men and ought to be received two or three hours at
after souper the quantity of. i.

Sief is a confectyon made after the fashion of a sugar lofe and most be
dyssoluyd in licour before it be receiuid

Collirium is a moist confection made of sief dissolved.

Sufuf is a fine powder made of diverse spices.

Secaniabin is a sharp syrup wherein is put sugar or honey.

Masticatoriu^ is a confection which is held in the mouth and chewed to purge
the head of phlegm.

Suffime^tum or suffumigatio is when diverse pouders be cast upon the cooles,
and the pacyent does receive the smoke thereof.

Gargarisme is a confectyon of diverse matters and sum decoctyon wherein sum
rob is dissolved, which is gargarised in the mouth and not swalowed down.

Here follow the compound medycynes which be applied to the outward parts of
the body.

UNgue^tu^ an ointme^t, is made of oils, spices and wax, and ought hot to be
applied to the place being sumwhat before rubbed with a lynen clothe.

Linimentu^ is in all points like to vngue^tu^ saving that there goes no wax
to the composityon thereof.

Emplastrum is made of herbs and spices, not being beatinge to powder but a
litel bruysed mixed with sum liquore or decoctyon, and being hot is put upon
a line^ cloth and so laid so laid to the sore.

Plus dyffereth not from an emplaster saving that mele or branne god to the
composityon thereof.

Cataplasma is made of grene herbs or dry sod in water till they be soft and
then applied to the sore.

Cerotu^ is made of wax or rosyn with oils and spyces, and is laid upon a cloth
cut after the form of the member it should be applied unto.

Dropax is an ointment only vsyd to take away hear.

Sinapismus is an emplaster made of mustard to vlcerate the skin and make the
same red.

Epithema is made of diverse pouders mixed with su^e ioice or distilled water, and
commonly laid upon skarlet is applied to the seek membre.

Embrocha is when the membre is washed gentilly with a spo^ge dypt in the
decoction of diverse herbs, rotes and flowers.

Fomentu^ is a bath made of the decoctyon of diverse herbs to wash the sore
place with al.

Euaporatio is when the diseased membre is holden in ye hot vapor of some
decoctyon.

Saceuly be bags made of linen cloth wherein be contained herbs rotes and
leaves which being hot must be first dypte in Wine or vinegar, and then
laid to the membre that is greuyd.

Encathisma or insessio is a decoctyon of certain things wherein ye pacyent
most sit for certain space.

The epistle of Diocles unto king Antigonus, which teaches a man to preserve
him self in health.
IN so much that your grace being now sumwhat run in years (most noble
Prince Antigonus) is endowed with knowl^dge above other kings, and that in all
parts of Phil^sophy and the arts called Mathematical wherein your grace has
wounderfully profited: I thought that part of Philosophy which teaches a man
to preserve himself in health not worthy to be despised and left untouched of
your regal majesty, wherefore I thought it necessari to declare unto your
majesty in this Epistle, the causes of diverse diseases with the signs and
tokens which goo before the same, and last of all the remedies wherwyth ^^e
same may be healed and cured, for like as the (...) no raginge and hideouse
tempest without sum^ ^anifest and open signs which declare the same to follow,
whereby men which have knowledge and be learned in ye Arcane and preuy works of
nature do so provide for themselves that they be sure from all perils and
i^operdyes that may ensue, so is there no kind of disease or sickness that may
infecte any membre of man's body but that has before such euydent signs
and tokens that it may be easlye known to follow. Therefore your grace puttyng
your trust and confidence in those our precepts may easly attain to the
perfect and absolute knowledge of all things.

First of all I have divided the body of man unto four parts, that is to say
the head, the breast, the belly, and the bladder.

Th^se signs and tokens do de^lare when any kind of disease is about to
infecte the head, daselyng in the eyes, the headache, heaviness of y^ brows, a
noise in the ears, prichinge in the temples, the eyes to water in the morninge
and the sight to fail, with dullness or want of smelling and the liftyng up of
the gummes.

When thou do perceive any such tokens, it is the best remedy to purge and
cleanse the head (and that with no purgatyue medycyne) but with, v. ounces of
wine made of wytheryd grapes, or of new wine sodde till half ^e wasted a way,
therewith thou shall wash t^y mouth fasting, and gargarise it therein till the
head be purged of phlegm therein contained, and this is the easyest remedy for all dyseasys in the head. Also it were very good and helthful, if the pacyent
fasting would eat a quantity of mustard which have been macerate or steped in
^at^r and honey myngled together, and gagarysynge the same would draw down the
humore contained in the head, but first of all yo^ most take heed the head be
coueryd tyill it h^ar, whereby the slymy phlegm may b^ made more apt and mere to
flow down to the mouth.

Now of the contrary part, whose despises these signs and tokens shall be
troubled with these deseases, or one of them, the ophtalmy, ye perle in the
ey^s, brekyng out about the cares poukes or weles in the neck, the c^nsumptyo^
in the brain, heuinesse in the head, the squina^ eye, worms which eat the
hear, the pains in the flape that coueryth the wind pype, the falling of
the hear, s^abbes or ulcers in the head, and the totheache.

You may perceive by these tokens if any man is like to be diseasyd about the
breast or no, first a swette through all the body and breast the tunge to wax
roughe or thyck^, the spittel to be salt or bitter in taste or choleric,
sodein pains in the sides or shulders without manifest occasyon, of tyaning
much watchynge, suffocatyones, thurst after sleep, great sadness, coldness
in the breast, and a shaking in the arms and hands, and the dyseases thereof
ensuing you may avoid with perbraking after a mean supper, without
receyuinge any medycyne. Also it is very good to vomit fasting,

Therefore let him that would vomit, eat Radyshe, Towneressys, Roket, Mustarde*
or purslane, and afterward drink warm wat^r and he shall vomit furthwith,
but he that serrythe lyt^ll by these presagyes and signs ought to fear these
diseasys, the pleurisy, pains in the longes, melancholical madness, sharp
agues, the phrenesy, the lythargye, and a burning ague with yeskynge.

When ye belly shall be dyseasyd, sum of these signs do comenly appear
before, the throws and pains in the belly, meats and drinks to ^^me bitter,
heuinesse in the knees, cold stiffness in the loins, weariness of all the
body without any occasyon, lack of senses in the legs, and easy fevers,
Now when ^riye of these tokens do appear it is best to make ye belly^ soft and
lose with some kind of dyete and with no purgi^g medicyne, for it is leasse
ieopardye to use such things that a man may skant err in, as betes sodde with
water and honey, sodde garlike, malowes, dockes, or mercurye and sweet metes
made with honey, for all these things do mollifye the belly, but if any of the
foresaid signs be manifest or endure long add to the said decoctyons the
joyce of b^stard Saffron, for thereby it shall be swetter and more wholesome. Also
Col^wortes sod in a great quantity of water, or four ounces of ye joyce thereof
receyuid with honey and salt, is very good, and of no less effect is the
water of the decoctyon of Cichepcasen or bitterfitch dronke fasting, But they
which think these signs to be of none effect, are oftentimes dyseased with
these syknesses, the flux in the belly, pains in ye bowelles, the lyenceri,
iliaca pa^sio which is a disease in the small guts, the ^ciatica, the fever
tertyan, the gout in ye feet, ye apoplexye the hemorrhoydes, and the ioynte
syknesse.

Al dyseases of the bladder, ^e known by these tokens, to be very full after
little meat, great in flatyons, much b^lc^ynge, the pale color of all the
body, heuye or sad sleep, vryne wane of color, and great pains in the
making there of, with swellyng about the pryuye members, after which tokens it
is good to use odoriferouse things which move urine, as the rotes of Fenel or
persely which have been steped a while in good and doriferouse white wine, of
yt which let the pacyent take every morning fasting three ounces with the water af
yelowe carettes or lonage or enula campana, for they be of like operation, and
of no less effica^y is ye water wherein Ciches have been steped in, if it be
drunk with wine. But whosoever does lyghtli passover these tokens shall look for
sum of these dyseases the hydropsye, the bygnesse of the spleen, pains in the
lyu^r, the stone, pains in the raynes, the strangurye, and the d^stentio^ of
the be^y. And her it is to be noted that in all these signs before rehearsed we
ought to mynister gentle and easy medecines to children, and to such as be
elder, medycynes that be of more strong operatyon and greater efficacye.

Now I entende brefly to declare unto your majesty the two turnynges of the
sone callid in latin solstitia (at which times such things do comenli chance)
and what meats your ^^ur grace shall use or absteyne from in either of them,
taking my beginning at the winter turnynge.

The winter turn.
Solu^itiu^ ^^emale which I call yt wi^ter turn is about ye xi. day of December
when the so^e enters the Goat.
IN the winter turn do rewmes and humiditie increase in me^nes bodies till ye
spri^g equinoctial, therefore it is good to eat who^e meats and to drink
sweet wynes and especially with wild marg^ram, and also to use ye company of
women.

There be from the winter turnynge to the spryng equinoctial nynty days.

The springtyme equinoctial.
From the spryng equinoctial unto the rysynge of the seven sterres called
vergiliac, does phlegm and swette corruptyon of the blood engendre in man's
body, The spring equinoctial is ye.x. day of March when the son enters the
Rame.
and for that cause it is good to use moist and tarte meats, to exercise ye
body, and not to absteyne from women, from the spring equinoctial to the
rysynge of pleyad^s be.xivi. days.

The rysynge of the seven stars.
Choler and vytter matter berythe rule in man from this time unto the somer
turnynge, The seven sters called vergilia^ or p^e^ades rise with the seen about
ye.ix day of may
therefore use meats that be sweet, laxatiue, and beware of acts venereal,
from the resig^e of p^e^ades unto the somer turn be xlv days.

The somer turnynge.
At this time is melancholye augmentyd tell the heruest equinoctial, therefore
drink cold water and smell odoriferouse things, The somer turn is about.x.
of July, when the sone enters the Crabbe.
and as for ^enus you most either use it moderatly or exchew it utterly, we
have to the heruest equinoctial nynty and three days.

The heruest equinoctial.
Phlegm and thine flurrons abound from this time to the setting of ye seuyn
sterres, The heruest equinoctial is about ye. 14 of Septe^bre when the son
enters the bala^ce.
therefore it is good to purge ye humors or to stop ye fluxyons, and to eat
al tarte and moist meats, to perbrake nothing at all, to excercyse ye body,
and to flee women, from which time to the setting of the seuin sterres
be.xxxvi. days.

The setting of the seven Sterres.
From this time to the winter turnynge does phlegm bear domynyon in man, The
seuyn sterres set with the sone about ye.x. of noue^bre
therefore you most eat fat and bitter things, drink sweet wynes, and
excercyse the body, from the going down of the.vii sterres till the Winter
turn be five and forty days.

Finis.
